<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8951766400661270932">Ten-year-old Annemarie Johansen and her best friend Ellen Rosen often think about life before the war. But it's now 1943 and their life in Copenhagen is filled with school, food shortages, and the Nazi soldiers marching in their town. <br /><br />The Nazis won't stop. The Jews of Denmark are being ”relocated,“ so Ellen moves in with the Johansens and pretends to be part of the family.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8951766400661270932">Ten-year-old Annemarie Johansen and her best friend Ellen Rosen often think about life before the war. But it's now 1943 and their life in Copenhagen is filled with school, food shortages, and the Nazi soldiers marching in their town. <br /><br />The Nazis won't stop. The Jews of Denmark are being ”relocated,“ so Ellen moves in with the Johansens and pretends to be part of the family. <br /><br />Then Annemarie is asked to go on a dangerous mission. Somehow she must find the strength and courage to save her best friend's life. There is no turning back now.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1786662" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/86145-stephanie" class="left imgcol" title="stephanie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1181278917p2/86145.jpg" alt="stephanie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1786662?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 17, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/86145-stephanie" class="user" title="stephanie">stephanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=prize-winners" class="actionLinkLite">prize-winners</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=would-rec" class="actionLinkLite">would-rec</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=good-more-than-once" class="actionLinkLite">good-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=holocaust" class="actionLinkLite">holocaust</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=childhood-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1786662">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15437013983479475353">i read this in hardback, when it first came out, and i'd say it was probably the reason i became addicted to WWII/holocaust literature/history at such a young age. <br /><br />i think it helped that i was so young when i read this, as imagining a ten year old standing up to nazis was something remarkable, but imaginable for me. i loved annemarie, i identified with her in ways i can't really explain. i read this book again and again, and it never changed. there are scenes burned into my memory: the fake fune</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15437013983479475353">i read this in hardback, when it first came out, and i'd say it was probably the reason i became addicted to WWII/holocaust literature/history at such a young age. <br /><br />i think it helped that i was so young when i read this, as imagining a ten year old standing up to nazis was something remarkable, but imaginable for me. i loved annemarie, i identified with her in ways i can't really explain. i read this book again and again, and it never changed. there are scenes burned into my memory: the fake funeral, the ripping of ellen's necklace, annemarie with the special packet, the idea of all the jews packed into uncle henrik's boat. and annemarie running, running fast like she did at school when she beat all the boys, running with a basket and a red cape (only later would i figure out the clever little red riding hood allusion), her blond hair trailing. <br /><br />it also helped that i had great-grandmothers who remembered the war, a swedish au pair who told me about seeing denmark from sweden, and an insatiable curiosity about things like this - so i was looking up things on maps and reading about german shepherds and the "scent rags" and. even when it was card-catalogs and old books, i was a cross referencer. i have notes somewhere of my favorite quotes from the book. <br /><br />i also love the ending - because it doesn't condescend. the ending, unlike the book, is ambigious in its ending. we know the war is over, we know annemarie survived - but what does that mean for a little girl, after all?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15437013983479475353">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16941784019898315091">I know- I can't believe I'm just now reading this. What kind of a children's librarian am I?<br /><br />This is a nice little story about a family who smuggles some Jewish friends out of Denmark during the Nazi occupation in 1943. I always avoided reading this because it looked depressing, but it wasn't. It wasn't a light story, but it didn't have the horrible scenes that fill most holocaust books.<br /><br />However, the author's note at the end affected me deeply. I don't know a lot about my Danish heritage- I've alw</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16941784019898315091">I know- I can't believe I'm just now reading this. What kind of a children's librarian am I?<br /><br />This is a nice little story about a family who smuggles some Jewish friends out of Denmark during the Nazi occupation in 1943. I always avoided reading this because it looked depressing, but it wasn't. It wasn't a light story, but it didn't have the horrible scenes that fill most holocaust books.<br /><br />However, the author's note at the end affected me deeply. I don't know a lot about my Danish heritage- I've always thought it was a sort of boring one. Most people I've known are descended from Danes, or some Scandinavian mix. Other than the Vikings, there's never seemed to be much of interest there. I've always envied my non-Scandinavian friends' more (in my mind) exotic backgrounds.<br /><br />I was amazed to read, though, of the courage and kindness of the Danes during WWII. The afterword spoke of the weeks in 1943 when the Danes smuggled almost their entire Jewish population out of Denmark- nearly 7000 people- to save them from the Nazi death camps. Astonishing. It makes me want to learn more about where I came from.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16941784019898315091">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/468484-presley" class="user" title="Presley">Presley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anybody!</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer10711818">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer360896480233925673">Number the Stars Bantam Doubleday Dell,1989, 152 pp., $5.99<br />Lois Lowery ISBN 0-06-447073-3<br /><br /> “Annemarie looked up, panting, just as she reached the corner. Her laughter stopped. Her heart seemed to skip a beat. ‘Halte!’ the soldier ordered in a stern voice ” (2, Lowery). And so begins Lois Lowery’s Number the Stars. When I first began to read Number the Stars a few years ago, I found that I could hardly get passed page three without dozing off. Recently, I had a friend tell me I should give the boo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText360896480233925673">Number the Stars 			 Bantam Doubleday Dell,1989, 152 pp., $5.99<br />Lois Lowery 				 ISBN 0-06-447073-3<br /><br />	“Annemarie looked up, panting, just as she reached the corner. Her laughter stopped. Her heart seemed to skip a beat. ‘Halte!’ the soldier ordered in a stern voice ” (2, Lowery). And so begins Lois Lowery’s Number the Stars. When I first began to read Number the Stars a few years ago, I found that I could hardly get passed page three without dozing off. Recently, I had a friend tell me I should give the book another chance. I decided to give it another go. This time around, I had a very different reaction and I couldn’t put the book down!<br />	The story is about a ten-year-old girl living in Copenhagen, Denmark during the Nazi invasion. Young Annemarie Johansen’s life is drastically altered, between her disappearing neighbors, rations on food and Nazi soldiers on every corner. When the invasion in her neighborhood begins to progress and get serious, Annemarie learns that the war is effecting her a lot more than she ever imagined it would. Her best friend’s family, the Rosens, are forced to separate for their safety, and Annemarie learns that when the world you live in needs improvements, bravery is always appreciated, regardless your age. <br />	At the beginning of the story, Annemarie seems used to and and accepting of the Nazi soldiers on every corner. By the end of the story she knew that there needed to be change and she would help in any way to make that happen. This included risking her life. <br />	Number the Stars is a gripping and moving novel that truly deserves its Newbery Medal. I would definitely recommend It grasps the reader and satisfies them with a suspenseful, sad and hopeful novel. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="360896480233925673">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7918444">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17553225489247166476">Is it just me, or do most books about Jewish girls during World War II suck? I'm serious, it's like this book and "Summer of my German Soldier" were written with the same purpose in mind: educate students about the Holocaust in just about the most boring way possible. Thank God there's the History Channel, or else my generation would've have thought the Holocaust as if it were simply a story about little girls and their twisted lives. I'm probably overexaggerating a bit, but ut's the best way I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17553225489247166476">Is it just me, or do most books about Jewish girls during World War II suck? I'm serious, it's like this book and "Summer of my German Soldier" were written with the same purpose in mind: educate students about the Holocaust in just about the most boring way possible. Thank God there's the History Channel, or else my generation would've have thought the Holocaust as if it were simply a story about little girls and their twisted lives. I'm probably overexaggerating a bit, but ut's the best way I can think to describe this book. How it ever won the Newberry Medal is beyond me. C'mon, the freaking climax of the book is when the main characher (Annemarie) skips through the forest, pretending to be Little Red Riding Hood. Yea, I go through 100-something pages to reach that. Yea, I'd like my money and my time back, please? Don't ever read this book.<br /><br />EDIT: How did this book get an award? It must have been a slow year the year it won.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1239323710">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5775561425552473696">I rarely read classic books nowadays. Seeing as my mom's idea of educational learning was to shove classic books down my throat (note: The first novel I finished reading was <a title="The Complete Sherlock Holmes by Arthur Conan Doyle" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/188572.The_Complete_Sherlock_Holmes">The Complete Sherlock Holmes</a> and I was fucking eight years old) I have to say that it's understandable if I steer clear of classics for awhile.<br /><br />The last classic novel I've read is this book. Mom is devious. She wrapped this little shit with a vintage wrapper, stashed it under my bed and asked me to clean my room because it re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5775561425552473696">I rarely read classic books nowadays. Seeing as my mom's idea of educational learning was to shove classic books down my throat (note: The first novel I finished reading was <a title="The Complete Sherlock Holmes by Arthur Conan Doyle" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/188572.The_Complete_Sherlock_Holmes">The Complete Sherlock Holmes</a> and I was fucking eight years old) I have to say that it's understandable if I steer clear of classics for awhile.<br /><br />The last classic novel I've read is this book. Mom is devious. She wrapped this little shit with a vintage wrapper, stashed it under my bed and asked me to clean my room because it resembles a pigsty. Of course, dutiful daughter that I am (ha!), I cleaned my room. While during the said activity, I saw something under my bed. (Guess what it is.) Our house is an old ancestral house and there's a lot of thing's I haven't seen yet at that house at the age of ten.So gullible me took the wrapped parcel and opened it. And lo and behold! It is a book! An old book with yellow crisp pages! I love old things and when you combine <strong> old + books </strong> you get a curious girl. So <strong> voila! </strong> I read it and loved it and reread it again and I was hooked.<br /><br /><br />Mom was happy.Dad is happy because Mom is happy. I was happy.The cat is happy because I was happy and the book is now missing because someone took it from my shelf.<br /><br /><strong>Happy ending.</strong></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1328024601">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15572554451836032500">4.5 stars for this jewel. One reason I enjoy historical fiction is the educational aspect; learning about something for the first time. This is not your typical WWII/Holocaust book. This one tells the story of how the Danish people, after their small country was invaded by Germany, smuggled nearly the entire population of Jews (7,000) across the sea to Sweden, saving them from deportation and almost certain death.<br /><br />The story is told through the eyes of 10 year old Annemarie Johansen, and how her f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15572554451836032500">4.5 stars for this jewel. One reason I enjoy historical fiction is the educational aspect; learning about something for the first time. This is not your typical WWII/Holocaust book. This one tells the story of how the Danish people, after their small country was invaded by Germany, smuggled nearly the entire population of Jews (7,000) across the sea to Sweden, saving them from deportation and almost certain death.<br /><br />The story is told through the eyes of 10 year old Annemarie Johansen, and how her family participated in the hiding and smuggling of the Jewish people, and their involvement in the Danish Resistance. Well done Lois Lowry. Winning the 1990 Newberry Medal for outstanding children's literature was well deserved.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_30294663">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30294663" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1431592-mulligan" class="left imgcol" title="Mulligan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1218904718p2/1431592.jpg" alt="Mulligan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/30294663?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 26, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1431592-mulligan" class="user" title="Mulligan">Mulligan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who like historical fiction and/or terrific characters</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer30294663">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15998355889263367945"><em>Number the Stars<em> by Lois Lowry takes place in Denmark during World War II and the Holocaust. The story begins with an introduction to the cruelty of German soldiers who are occupying Denmark, the story's heroine, Annemarie, her younger (and more bratty), and her best friend Ellen Rosen. From there, this young adult novel tells a tale of bravery.<br /><br />Soon after the beginning of the story, the Nazi soldiers begin attempting to take Denmark's Jewish citizens away to concentration camps (read: starvation</em></em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15998355889263367945"><em>Number the Stars<em> by Lois Lowry takes place in Denmark during World War II and the Holocaust. The story begins with an introduction to the cruelty of German soldiers who are occupying Denmark, the story's heroine, Annemarie, her younger (and more bratty), and her best friend Ellen Rosen. From there, this young adult novel tells a tale of bravery.<br /><br />Soon after the beginning of the story, the Nazi soldiers begin attempting to take Denmark's Jewish citizens away to concentration camps (read: starvation and eventual death). As this happens, other Danish citizens and members of a secret movement, the Resistance, protect their Jewish neighbors and begin smuggling them to safety in Sweden. Eventually, Annemarie's family smuggle Ellen Rosen, a young Jewish girl, to their relative's house near Sweden. It is there that the story unfolds and the suspense begins. <br /><br />One of the best things about <em>Number the Stars<em>, for me, was the way Annemarie demonstrated quiet bravery in the face of danger. Her character showed that it doesn't take brute strength and power to be a hero. Because of that message alone (and maybe also the simple, but beautiful writing), I would highly recommend this book.</em></em></em></em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15998355889263367945">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_38647833">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38647833" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/612636-beth" class="left imgcol" title="Beth"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1447971489p2/612636.jpg" alt="Beth" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38647833?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 13, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/612636-beth" class="user" title="Beth">Beth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/612636-beth?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/612636-beth?shelf=newbery" class="actionLinkLite">newbery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38647833">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2094393327495436376">On the back of the library's copy of this book is a review from The Horn Book Magazine that says "the whole book is seamless, compelling, and memorable -- impossible to put down; difficult to forget." Well, I was about to put that bold statement to the test: "difficult to forget," huh? What if you read this twenty years ago and have had two kids and subsequent serious sleep deprivation since then??<br /><br />Well, I can't remember items on my shopping list while I'm at the store, but I remembered a surpris</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2094393327495436376">On the back of the library's copy of this book is a review from The Horn Book Magazine that says "the whole book is seamless, compelling, and memorable -- impossible to put down; difficult to forget." Well, I was about to put that bold statement to the test: "difficult to forget," huh? What if you read this twenty years ago and have had two kids and subsequent serious sleep deprivation since then??<br /><br />Well, I can't remember items on my shopping list while I'm at the store, but I remembered a surprising number of details from this book once I started reading: the whole first scene of the three girls being stopped by Nazi soldiers on a Copenhagen street corner, the image of the Star of David charm imprinting itself on Annamarie's hand, the climactic walk to the fishing boat and being stopped by the soldiers with dogs. The scenes that had been subconsciously hidden in my mind for years unearthed themselves as I turned the pages -- indeed, it is a memorable book.<br /><br />The story is a courageous tale of fictional ten-year-old Annemarie -- and of the real citizens of World War II Denmark, who swiftly united to smuggle their Jewish population to Sweden, which was well worth learning about. Additionally, the writing is superb: somehow, Lowry manages to weave detail and plot together in a way that enriches young (and old) readers while not overwhelming them. Each word, each scene is crafted as though this were a poem rather than a novel-- don't be deceived by the thinness of this little book.<br /><br />Loved this book even more than I did in elementary school. It was definitely worth revisiting.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2094393327495436376">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/1653142-jennifer" class="user" title="Jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36120854">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3274723193966367988">I love books about WWII and this has been one of my favorites since I read it in 6th grade!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_86213116">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86213116" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/307208-lucy" class="left imgcol" title="Lucy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1233177432p2/307208.jpg" alt="Lucy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/86213116?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 21, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/307208-lucy" class="user" title="Lucy">Lucy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer86213116">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9064811876710253035">I love Lois Lowry. The Giver is one of my all-time favorite books. She has a way of explaining a complex idea or lesson in a simple, but not at all dumbed down way. Lowry's story of a young girl living in Denmark during the Nazi occupation, and trying to understand who the Nazis are and what their presence means does just that. When Annemarie Johansen's best friend, Ellen Rose,who is Jewish, moves in with her family and pretends to be her dead sister because her parents are forced to go into hid</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9064811876710253035">I love Lois Lowry. The Giver is one of my all-time favorite books. She has a way of explaining a complex idea or lesson in a simple, but not at all dumbed down way. Lowry's story of a young girl living in Denmark during the Nazi occupation, and trying to understand who the Nazis are and what their presence means does just that. When Annemarie Johansen's best friend, Ellen Rose,who is Jewish, moves in with her family and pretends to be her dead sister because her parents are forced to go into hiding in order to avoid being "relocated", the questions that arise about why the secrecy is necessary becomes a perfect first exposure to a young reader not experienced with the brutality and horror of the holocaust. Lowry doesn't shy away from any of the fear, cowardliness, bravery, anger, deception, confusion, or strength shown by those who lived through this dark time in history. However, she unfolds the story through the eyes of ten year-old Annemarie so the story is appropriate for that age group. <br /><br />I think this is the very best of young adult or children's literature. Compelling, honest, well-written and important. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9064811876710253035">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer12873548">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13879662038910114080">This wonderful story about a Danish family involved in rescuing their Jewish friends from the Nazis is a good—-and relatively gentle—-introduction to the Holocaust for young children. It’s hard not to be inspired over and over by the incredible moral courage of the Danish people and the strong moral leadership provided by the king, the military, and law enforcement. I wish this book had been around when I was a child. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1098120737">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098120737" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18882907-jaseena-al" class="left imgcol" title="Jaseena AL"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448347215p2/18882907.jpg" alt="Jaseena AL" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/1098120737?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18882907-jaseena-al" class="user" title="Jaseena AL">Jaseena AL</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18882907-jaseena-al?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18882907-jaseena-al?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18882907-jaseena-al?shelf=realistic-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1098120737">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2820313206259800391"><br />Title: Number The Stars<br />Type: Standalone<br />Author: Lois Lowry<br />Release Date: Feb 9,1998<br />Rating: 4 stars<br /><br />“And they are beginning to realize that the world they live in is a place where the right thing is often hard, sometimes dangerous, and frequently unpopular.<br /><br />Few lines from the letter of a young Danish Resistance leader kim Malthe-Bruun to his mother the night before he was executed.<br /><br /> “...<em>and I want you all to remember-that you must not dream yourselves back to the times before the war, but the dream fo</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2820313206259800391"><br />Title: Number The Stars<br />Type: Standalone<br />Author: Lois Lowry<br />Release Date: Feb 9,1998<br />Rating: 4 stars<br /><br />“And they are beginning to realize that the world they live in is a place where the right thing is often hard, sometimes dangerous, and frequently unpopular.<br /><br />Few lines from the letter of a young Danish Resistance leader kim Malthe-Bruun to his mother the night before he was executed.<br /><br /> “...<em>and I want you all to remember-that you must not dream yourselves back to the times before the war, but the dream for you all, young and old, must be to create an ideal of human decency, and not a narrow-minded and prejudiced one. That is the great gift our country hungers for, something every little peasant boy can look forward to, and with pleasure feel he is a part of-something he can work and fight for<em>."<br /><br />Number The Stars is set in a tragic era in the history of mankind Denmark in 1943, during World War II.Denmark was under Nazi Occupation from 1943-1948 . The story revolves around 10 year old Annemarie Johansen and her Jewish friend Ellen Rosen and their families.Life in Denmark was very difficult during that time.Nazi soldiers were on every nooke and corner of the city. There were no enough food ,beverages or clothing for anyone and they were required to darken their windows after 8:00.Annemaries’s and Ellen’s families were very close. One the day of Jewish New year Ellen’s parent received a word from the church that all the Jewish families in Denmark were to be taken and ‘’relocated’’.Since then Ellen’s parents Mr. and Mrs. Rosen went hiding leaving Ellen with Annemaries’s family.Ellen pretended to be Annemaries’s late sister Lise when the soldiers came searching for the Rosens in Annemarie's apartment. Later that day Mrs. Johansen takes her two daughters and Ellen to her house in the north coast of Denmark where with the help of Peter Neilson,fiance of her late sister,Lise and her uncle Henrick helps them to escape to Sweden.In a great effort led by Peter, Denmark manages to smuggle almost the entire Jewish population (7,000 people) into Sweden, a Nazi-free country.<br /><br />Peter Neilson was later captured and executed by the Germans.Annemarie also learns that her late sister Lise was also in the resistance along with Peter and was shot by the Nazi’s.This book is all about the trouble they had to encounter and courage Annemarie had to show to help the Jewish families. <br /><br />Number The Star is written in a simple language making it easy for children to understand.There were at times when there was no logic in what they were doing,like how Mr Rosen had to take the ‘’packet’’ to Mr. Henrick when Peter could have directly handed it to him.<br /><br />I would rate this book Four out of five stars.</em></em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2820313206259800391">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_491831821">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/491831821" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2624836-reese" class="left imgcol" title="Reese"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452146059p2/2624836.jpg" alt="Reese" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/491831821?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2624836-reese" class="user" title="Reese">Reese</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6091080-number-the-stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440700319" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer491831821">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9843098125530014297">Have I ever looked at any reviews shortly before I typed my own comments about a book? I don't think so -- that is, until a few minutes ago. In countless ways, reviewers offered the same basic "confession": only years after its publication did I finally get around to reading Lois Lowry's <em> Number the Stars </em>. So perhaps I shouldn't feel embarrassed by my failure to read this Newberry Award Medal Winner until just about twenty-five years after its release. I can't account for its not having been in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9843098125530014297">Have I ever looked at any reviews shortly before I typed my own comments about a book? I don't think so -- that is, until a few minutes ago. In countless ways, reviewers offered the same basic "confession": only years after its publication did I finally get around to reading Lois Lowry's <em> Number the Stars </em>. So perhaps I shouldn't feel embarrassed by my failure to read this Newberry Award Medal Winner until just about twenty-five years after its release. I can't account for its not having been in my hands when I was still reading to my children, who, during the 1990s, were an appropriate audience for the work. If I had read the book to my children, the number of stars in my rating would probably have been five. It is truly, for many reasons, one of those books that I SHOULD have read aloud to "Goldilocks" children, meaning not too young and not too old to hear me read it. <br /><br />Despite the regrets about having been late in reaching for it, I certainly don't regret having eventually read it. For those who may never become acquainted with it, I feel obliged to record the words of Kim Malthe-Brunn, one of Denmark's Resistance leaders executed by the Nazis. Lowry, in her "Afterword," includes part of a letter that he wrote the night before his execution: "I want you all to remember -- that you must not dream yourselves back to the times before the war, but the dream for you all, young and old, must be to create an ideal of human decency, and not a narrow-minded and prejudiced one"(137). Even if heroic acts never become a chapter of my life, I believe that I will remember to read to a new generation of young people words that can move us closer to civilized conduct and away from barbarism. Can't each of us at least do that? <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9843098125530014297">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/2095554-peachy?shelf=wwii" class="actionLinkLite">wwii</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2095554-peachy?shelf=inspirational" class="actionLinkLite">inspirational</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2095554-peachy?shelf=family" class="actionLinkLite">family</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48233721">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10826541944701682215">Number The Stars is a heartening tale of the solidarity and love shared by a country and her countrymen, even whereby divergent religions could cause no fault. It is a tale woven with endearing and inspiring characters, written in a simple yet poignant manner, by one of the most affecting Young-Adult Fiction writers of our time. Lowry is a master in the art of the subtle details that invoke elaborate and griping visualizations. The prose is ever engaging as the depictions of beautiful scenery ar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10826541944701682215">Number The Stars is a heartening tale of the solidarity and love shared by a country and her countrymen, even whereby divergent religions could cause no fault. It is a tale woven with endearing and inspiring characters, written in a simple yet poignant manner, by one of the most affecting Young-Adult Fiction writers of our time. Lowry is a master in the art of the subtle details that invoke elaborate and griping visualizations. The prose is ever engaging as the depictions of beautiful scenery are juxtaposed by brutal content, as is unconditional love of man by another’s opportunistic hatred, and innate kindness by enforced cruelty. <br /><br /><br /><br />Through our protagonist, Annemarie, we are met with candid innocence, as with her admiration of Sweden among other things, she is always hopeful and virtuously in search of freedom. In a child who is courageous enough to admit and face her fears, we learn the true meaning of bravery and what it means personally and as a whole. <br /><br /><br /><br />This moving piece of fiction is one part, history lesson, and two parts, a lesson in humanity, and I encourage all tweens, teens and adults that haven’t had the opportunity to read it to lend themselves to its splendor. <br /><br /><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.booksnakereviews.blogspot.com" target="_blank">www.booksnakereviews.blogspot.com</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10826541944701682215">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6218495">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6218495" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="left imgcol" title="Briynne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1225157665p2/94054.jpg" alt="Briynne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6218495?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/94054-briynne" class="user" title="Briynne">Briynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6218495">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12304606704334351281">I read this book compulsively as a child. It was my introduction to the Holocaust. Like so many book-nerds, I read precociously and therefore got to a lot of books before I reached the prescribed grade-level. So, I read this book before the words "World War" or "genocide" ever reached my ears in a classroom. I was fascinated by it all in a very child-like way. I couldn't really understand why the Rosens were in danger, so when Annemarie's father explains the whole thing to her, he was explaining</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12304606704334351281">I read this book compulsively as a child. It was my introduction to the Holocaust. Like so many book-nerds, I read precociously and therefore got to a lot of books before I reached the prescribed grade-level. So, I read this book before the words "World War" or "genocide" ever reached my ears in a classroom. I was fascinated by it all in a very child-like way. I couldn't really understand why the Rosens were in danger, so when Annemarie's father explains the whole thing to her, he was explaining it to me as well. Growing up in the middle of nowhere, Michigan, I had never met a Jewish person in my life; they were, to me, nice people who lived in deserts in stories from Sunday school. They seemed like very unlikely subjects for hatred to me, and I felt quite sorry for Ellen and her family. <br /><br />It is, thankfully, a gentle book that doesn't really scratch the surface of what happened; I couldn't have handled pits of emaciated bodies or savagery. The fairly tame shootings and violence in the book unnerved me enough as it was. It takes place in occupied Amsterdam, not Berlin, and that war-time provincialism also helps de-intensify the subject matter. Most importantly, it's told through the view of a child, which I think speaks the most vividly to other children. An excellent book that could easily be required grade school reading. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12304606704334351281">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_115696598">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115696598" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2604014-carol" class="left imgcol" title="Carol"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1250312351p2/2604014.jpg" alt="Carol" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/115696598?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2604014-carol" class="user" title="Carol">Carol</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer115696598">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13582587422094087366">I loved Lowry's The Giver and always wanted to read this one. OMG she is such an excellent writer, and was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1990. Number the Stars is a work of historical fiction about the escape of a Jewish family from Copenhagen during Occupation of Denmark during the Second World War because of the Holocaust. The story centers around ten-year-old Annemarie Johansen, who lived in Copenhagen, Denmark, in 1943 and was caught up in the events surrounding the rescue of the Danish Jews.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13582587422094087366">I loved Lowry's The Giver and always wanted to read this one. OMG she is such an excellent writer, and was awarded the Newbery Medal in 1990. Number the Stars is a work of historical fiction about the escape of a Jewish family from Copenhagen during Occupation of Denmark during the Second World War because of the Holocaust. The story centers around ten-year-old Annemarie Johansen, who lived in Copenhagen, Denmark, in 1943 and was caught up in the events surrounding the rescue of the Danish Jews. She risks her life to help her best friend, Ellen Rosen, by pretending that Ellen is Annemarie's older sister. Annemarie's older sister had died earlier in the war as a result of her work with the Danish Resistance. The story's title is taken from a reference to Psalm 147, in which the writer of the book relates that God has numbered all the stars in the universe. It is meant to tie into the Star of David, specifically to Ellen's necklace, which is symbolic to the story.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13582587422094087366">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7696163387438128139">My wife read this when she was around 10 years old, while I was reading other things, I guess. I have two daughters and want to be able to recommend them good books when they are old enough, so I wanted to make up for lost time and read some good children's literature. This is very good for a someone in the 3rd, 4th, or 5th grade. <br /><br />Lowry is vague on the facts of WWII, which was OK with me because I hate it when authors break the flow of the story to give a history lesson. She tells a good tale an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7696163387438128139">My wife read this when she was around 10 years old, while I was reading other things, I guess. I have two daughters and want to be able to recommend them good books when they are old enough, so I wanted to make up for lost time and read some good children's literature. This is very good for a someone in the 3rd, 4th, or 5th grade. <br /><br />Lowry is vague on the facts of WWII, which was OK with me because I hate it when authors break the flow of the story to give a history lesson. She tells a good tale and keeps tension throughout. She shows us bravery, loyalty, and friendship without getting heavy handed. I will recommend it to my kids for sure.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a href="/review/show/1328660785?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21785635-rue" class="user" title="Rue">Rue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1328660785">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2834190424608699076">This book did things to my heart. I read it when I was ten, which is the age of the main character in this book, and I was literally taken back to Amsterdam in World War 2. When Annemarie was scared, so was I. When she felt happy, I did too. Probably one of my favourite books of all time. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/285517445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6974796-kritika-swarup" class="user" title="Kritika Swarup">Kritika Swarup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47281.Number_the_Stars" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440227533" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer285517445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11701510609207159255">Independence is a precious gift. A story of war brings back the realization multiplied to leave a sharp impact. The book emphasises on treasuring harmony while quoting from a letter written by a Danish Resistance leader a night before his execution:<br /><br />"..you must not dream yourselves to the times before the war, but the dream for you all, young and old, must be to create an ideal of human decency, and not a narrow minded and prejudiced one.."<br /><br />While reading an account of struggle captures the reader</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11701510609207159255">Independence is a precious gift. A story of war brings back the realization multiplied to leave a sharp impact. The book emphasises on treasuring harmony while quoting from a letter written by a Danish Resistance leader a night before his execution:<br /><br />"..you must not dream yourselves to the times before the war, but the dream for you all, young and old, must be to create an ideal of human decency, and not a narrow minded and prejudiced one.."<br /><br />While reading an account of struggle captures the reader in that world, the writer I assume congratulates herself to have delivered the promise. The idea of putting a small girl at the centre of the story is not an innovative trick but to deliver that innocence, imagination, apprehension and courage in the same soft and chaste tone to appeal to the audience decides the success of the writing.<br /><br />While the imaginative descriptions of the countries and locations did an excellent job in leaving behind memorable imprints, I for a moment amused myself with the thought of having learnt the entire geography through such descriptions. Then I wouldn't have feared that subject, maybe! :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11701510609207159255">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2493.Lois_Lowry">About Lois Lowry</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/2493.Lois_Lowry"><img alt="2493" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1348162077p2/2493.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16612117105072632154">Taken from Lowry's website:<br />"I’ve always felt that I was fortunate to have been born the middle child of three. My older sister, Helen, was very much like our mother: gentle, family-oriented, eager to please. Little brother Jon was the only boy and had interests that he shared with Dad; together they were always working on electric trains and erector sets; and later, when Jon was older, they always</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16612117105072632154">Taken from Lowry's website:<br />"I’ve always felt that I was fortunate to have been born the middle child of three. My older sister, Helen, was very much like our mother: gentle, family-oriented, eager to please. Little brother Jon was the only boy and had interests that he shared with Dad; together they were always working on electric trains and erector sets; and later, when Jon was older, they always seemed to have their heads under the raised hood of a car. That left me in-between, and exactly where I wanted most to be: on my own. I was a solitary child who lived in the world of books and my own vivid imagination.<br /><br />Because my father was a career military officer - an Army dentist - I lived all over the world. I was born in Hawaii, moved from there to New York, spent the years of World War II in my mother’s hometown: Carlisle, Pennsylvania, and from there went to Tokyo when I was eleven. High school was back in New York City, but by the time I went to college (Brown University in Rhode Island), my family was living in Washington, D.C.<br /><br />I married young. I had just turned nineteen - just finished my sophomore year in college - when I married a Naval officer and continued the odyssey that military life requires. California. Connecticut (a daughter born there). Florida (a son). South Carolina. Finally Cambridge, Massachusetts, when my husband left the service and entered Harvard Law School (another daughter; another son) and then to Maine - by now with four children under the age of five in tow. My children grew up in Maine. So did I. I returned to college at the University of Southern Maine, got my degree, went to graduate school, and finally began to write professionally, the thing I had dreamed of doing since those childhood years when I had endlessly scribbled stories and poems in notebooks.<br /><br />After my marriage ended in 1977, when I was forty, I settled into the life I have lived ever since. Today I am back in Cambridge, Massachusetts, living and writing in a house dominated by a very shaggy Tibetan Terrier named Bandit. For a change of scenery Martin and I spend time in Maine, where we have an old (it was built in 1768!) farmhouse on top of a hill. In Maine I garden, feed birds, entertain friends, and read...<br /><br />My books have varied in content and style. Yet it seems that all of them deal, essentially, with the same general theme: the importance of human connections. A Summer to Die, my first book, was a highly fictionalized retelling of the early death of my sister, and of the effect of such a loss on a family. Number the Stars, set in a different culture and era, tells the same story: that of the role that we humans play in the lives of our fellow beings.<br /><br />The Giver - and Gathering Blue, and the newest in the trilogy: Messenger - take place against the background of very different cultures and times. Though all three are broader in scope than my earlier books, they nonetheless speak to the same concern: the vital need of people to be aware of their interdependence, not only with each other, but with the world and its environment.<br /><br />My older son was a fighter pilot in the United States Air Force. His death in the cockpit of a warplane tore away a piece of my world. But it left me, too, with a wish to honor him by joining the many others trying to find a way to end conflict on this very fragile earth.<br />I am a grandmother now. For my own grandchildren - and for all those of their generation - I try, through writing, to convey my passionate awareness that we live intertwined on this planet and that our future depends upon our caring more, and doing more, for one another."</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16612117105072632154">...more</a>

    </div>
